## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving), following Newton's second law with nonlinear force terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear damping and restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) * x (parametric + nonlinear)
- Velocity-dependent restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v**2 (coupling between position and velocity)
- Driven Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven self-excited oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential well / symmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Even-power position terms (x**2) in restoring force → asymmetric potential well, indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v → self-excited oscillation with amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Cosine or sine functions of time → external periodic driving force; frequency and amplitude are key parameters
- Product terms x*v or x**2*v → nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x**3) → double-well potential / bistability
- Odd-power velocity terms (v**3) → nonlinear drag forces (e.g., turbulent damping)
- Time-dependent coefficient multiplying x → parametric excitation, can lead to parametric resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Position-velocity product x*v → can arise from coordinate transformations or conservative nonlinear coupling
